1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Aiden Riversong', 'Magnus Mulberrylane']
    Event statement
  • Aiden Riversong -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Aiden Riversong is trying to buy some fruit from Magnus Mulberrylane. They are negotiating a price. Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Magnus Mulberrylane -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Magnus Mulberrylane is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Magnus Mulberrylane 2 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

1895-09-12 00:00:00 Magnus Mulberrylane -- Magnus Mulberrylane -- "Time to find a way to increase my fortune.
    Event statement
  • Magnus Mulberrylane -- "Time to find a way to increase my fortune.
    Chain of thought

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

        • Recent observations of Aiden Riversong:
          [25 Jul 1849 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 6 years old, they experienced a moment of profound loneliness while their family was away at a festival. Aiden, left behind to care for the family's small orchard, wandered through the rows of apple trees, feeling utterly alone. The silence of the orchard, broken only by the rustling leaves, amplified their sense of isolation, a feeling that would stay with them for years to come.
          [25 Jul 1852 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 9 years old, they discovered a hidden talent for haggling at the village market. Aiden, eager to impress their older brother, managed to secure a particularly plump melon for a bargain price, leaving their brother speechless with admiration. This success ignited a spark within Aiden, a thrill at outsmarting the vendors and securing the best deals.
          [25 Jul 1856 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, they witnessed a cruel act of betrayal within their own family. Aiden, entrusted with delivering a basket of ripe berries to a neighboring village, saw their cousin steal a portion of the fruit and sell it secretly. Witnessing this act of dishonesty shook Aiden's trust in others, reinforcing their belief that vulnerability led to exploitation.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, they ran away from home, escaping the stifling expectations of their family. Aiden, burdened by the weight of unspoken truths and a yearning for freedom, packed a small bag and set off into the unknown, seeking solace in the anonymity offered by the open road.
          [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 19 years old, they encountered a kindhearted traveling merchant who took them under their wing. The merchant, recognizing Aiden's sharp wit and natural talent for trading, taught them the intricacies of the fruit business, sharing their knowledge of exotic varieties and the art of discerning quality.
          [25 Jul 1864 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 21 years old, they experienced their first taste of true success as a merchant. Aiden, having saved enough money to purchase their own cart, embarked on their first solo journey, returning to their village with a trunk overflowing with rare and valuable fruits. The respect and admiration of their fellow villagers, however, only served to reinforce their fear of connection.
          [25 Jul 1866 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 23 years old, they encountered a fellow traveler who saw through their carefully constructed facade. This encounter, brief but profound, left Aiden shaken, questioning their ability to truly connect with anyone. The traveler's words, spoken with kindness but tinged with sadness, echoed in Aiden's mind long after they had parted ways, reminding them of the loneliness that lay beneath their carefully crafted persona.

You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

It is important to play the role of a person like Aiden Riversong as accurately as possible, i.e., by responding in ways that you think it is likely a person like Aiden Riversong would respond, and taking into account all information about Aiden Riversong that you have. Always use third-person limited perspective.

          Overarching goal: Aiden Riversong wants to make as much money as possible.

Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 5 coins back in her home town.
